Antoine Dupont had one ambition when he switched his focus to what he described as the French Olympic project: a gold medal for the host nation.\n\nParis, Jul 23 (AP) Antoine Dupont had one ambition when he switched his focus to what he described as the French Olympic project: a gold medal for the host nation.\n\nThe world's premier rugby player will get France's Olympic medal campaign underway Wednesday, two days before the official opening ceremony of the Paris Games, when his team takes on the United States in the first Pool B game of the rugby sevens competition.\n\nAlso Read | Most Medals Won By An Athlete in Olympics and Other Major Records in History of Multi-Sport Mega Event Ahead of Paris Olympic Games 2024.\n\nStade de France will be at capacity and most of the attention will be on Dupont when the French kick off in the third game of a three-day men's tournament. It'll be the same on Day 2 when the French meet two-time Olympic champion Fiji, the most formidable force in rugby's condensed sevens format.\n\nThe U.S. men face France and Fiji on Wednesday, giving them a unique view of a pair of title favorites.\n\nAlso Read | MLC 2024: San Francisco Unicorns Hand Washington Freedom Their First Defeat of the Season, Win Match by 6 Wickets.\n\n\"When we get in that environment, besides maybe 14 players, give or take 50 friends and family coming in supporting us, the staff and the people watching on TV -- we know it's going to be us versus 69,000 people,\" U.S. captain Kevon Williams said of facing the French. \"We're OK with that, we've been preparing for that, we've honed in and said, It's just us.'\n\n\"All we'll see is the French jersey, so we'll be ready.\"\n\nFrance hosted the Rugby World Cup last year and the national team again failed to lift the title. It has been a finalist three times at the sport's biggest tournament.\n\nWith undisputed star of the 15-a-side game joining its ranks, France has peaked in the rugby sevens format in 2024. Dupont helped the French win a spot on the world series for the first time in 19 years, and then capped it with a victory in the series finale in Madrid.\n\nThe French evolution has coincided with an unusually lean season for Fiji.\n\nAlthough Fiji head coach Osea Kolinisau is confident the team's bid for an Olympic three-peat will overshadow the inconsistent world series run by the time the men's sevens medals are awarded Saturday.\n\n\"We plan to keep that legacy going,\" Kolinisau said. \"We can claim it solely.\"\n\nKolinisau led Fiji to its first ever Olympic gold medal as captain in 2016 at Rio de Janeiro, where rugby sevens was featured on the Olympic program for the first time.\n\nKolinisau was rushed into the coaching role earlier this year to resurrect Fiji's men's program, and he reinstated what he calls the \"Fijian way\" -- or instinct -- for sevens rugby: \"High tempo, high risk.\"\n\nIn the series finale, the Fijians posted wins over Ireland, South Africa and New Zealand before losing to France in the semifinals.\n\nFor Argentina, a grand final loss to France in Madrid was a setback after it topped the league stage of the world series, winning three of the seven stops.\n\nFor the Olympic tournament, Argentina is grouped with Australia, Samoa and Kenya in Pool B. No. 2-ranked Ireland, Tokyo silver medalist New Zealand, Rio bronze medalist South Africa and Japan are in a tough Pool A. Uruguay joins France, Fiji and the U.S. in Pool C.\n\nThe top two teams in each group and the two best third-place teams advance to the quarterfinals, meaning two-thirds of the 12 starters are still in medal contention when the knockout phase starts.\n\nThat's the stage where the Fijians have come into their own at the two previous Olympics.\n\nJerry Tuwai has been integral in Fiji's first two Olympic runs and the 35-year-old playmaker was recalled by Kolinisau two months ago after almost a year out of the team.\n\nA two-time Olympic champion, Sevens World Cup winner and player of the decade, Tuwai has embraced Kolinisau's approach ahead of the Paris Games.\n\n\"Our style of play has been opened up and our teamwork and communication. Our decision making -- that's another thing that opened up, too,\" Tuwai said. \"After two Olympic gold medals, these boys have shown they always show up in very big tournaments.\n\n\"We have this It'll be the same on Day 2 when the French meet two-time Olympic champion Fiji, the most formidable force in rugby's condensed sevens format.\n\nThe U.S. men face France and Fiji on Wednesday, giving them a unique view of a pair of title favorites.\n\n\"When we get in that environment, besides maybe 14 players, give or take 50 friends and family coming in supporting us, the staff and the people watching on TV -- we know it's going to be us versus 69,000 people,\" U.S. captain Kevon Williams said of facing the French. \"We're OK with that, we've been preparing for that, we've honed in and said, 'It's just us.'\n\n\"All we'll see is the French jersey, so we'll be ready.\"\n\nFrance hosted the Rugby World Cup last year and the national team again failed to lift the title. It has been a finalist three times at the sport's biggest tournament.\n\nWith undisputed star of the 15-a-side game joining its ranks, France has peaked in the rugby sevens format in 2024. Dupont helped the French win a spot on the world series for the first time in 19 years, and then capped it with a victory in the series finale in Madrid.\n\nThe French evolution has coincided with an unusually lean season for Fiji.\n\nAlthough Fiji head coach Osea Kolinisau is confident the team's bid for an Olympic three-peat will overshadow the inconsistent world series run by the time the men's sevens medals are awarded Saturday.\n\n\"We plan to keep that legacy going,\" Kolinisau said. \"We can claim it solely.\"\n\nKolinisau led Fiji to its first ever Olympic gold medal as captain in 2016 at Rio de Janeiro, where rugby sevens was featured on the Olympic program for the first time.\n\nKolinisau was rushed into the coaching role earlier this year to resurrect Fiji's men's program, and he reinstated what he calls the \"Fijian way\" -- or instinct -- for sevens rugby: \"High tempo, high risk.\"\n\nIn the series finale, the Fijians posted wins over Ireland, South Africa and New Zealand before losing to France in the semifinals.\n\nFor Argentina, a grand final loss to France in Madrid was a setback after it topped the league stage of the world series, winning three of the seven stops.\n\nFor the Olympic tournament, Argentina is grouped with Australia, Samoa and Kenya in Pool B. No. 2-ranked Ireland, Tokyo silver medalist New Zealand, Rio bronze medalist South Africa and Japan are in a tough Pool A. Uruguay joins France, Fiji and the U.S. in Pool C.\n\nThe top two teams in each group and the two best third-place teams advance to the quarterfinals, meaning two-thirds of the 12 starters are still in medal contention when the knockout phase starts.\n\nThat's the stage where the Fijians have come into their own at the two previous Olympics.\n\nJerry Tuwai has been integral in Fiji's first two Olympic runs and the 35-year-old playmaker was recalled by Kolinisau two months ago after almost a year out of the team.\n\nA two-time Olympic champion, Sevens World Cup winner and player of the decade, Tuwai has embraced Kolinisau's approach ahead of the Paris Games.\n\n\"Our style of play has been opened up and our teamwork and communication. Our decision making -- that's another thing that opened up, too,\" Tuwai said. \"After two Olympic gold medals, these boys have shown they always show up in very big tournaments.\n\n\"We have this Osea Kolinisau led Fiji to its first ever Olympic gold medal when rugby sevens made its debut at the Summer Games in 2016 and now, as a coach, he's turning to old teammate Jerry Tuwai to help the Pacific nation's bid for a three-peat.\n\nAntoine Dupont had one ambition when he switched his focus to what he described as the French Olympic project: a gold medal for the host nation.\n\nThe world's premier rugby player will get France's Olympic medal campaign underway Wednesday, two days before the official opening ceremony of the Paris Games, when his team takes on the United States in the first Pool B game of the rugby sevens competition.\n\nStade de France will be at capacity and most of the attention will be on Dupont when the French kick off in the third game of a three-day men's tournament. It has been a finalist three times at the sport's biggest tournament.\n\nWith undisputed star of the 15-a-side game joining its ranks, France has peaked in the rugby sevens format in 2024. Dupont helped the French win a spot on the world series for the first time in 19 years, and then capped it with a victory in the series finale in Madrid.\n\nThe French evolution has coincided with an unusually lean season for Fiji.\n\nAlthough Fiji head coach Osea Kolinisau is confident the team's bid for an Olympic three-peat will overshadow the inconsistent world series run by the time the men's sevens medals are awarded Saturday.\n\n\"We plan to keep that legacy going,\" Kolinisau said. \"We can claim it solely.\"\n\nKolinisau led Fiji to its first ever Olympic gold medal as captain in 2016 at Rio de Janeiro, where rugby sevens was featured on the Olympic program for the first time.\n\nKolinisau was rushed into the coaching role earlier this year to resurrect Fiji's men's program, and he reinstated what he calls the \"Fijian way\" -- or instinct -- for sevens rugby: \"High tempo, high risk.\"\n\nIn the series finale, the Fijians posted wins over Ireland, South Africa and New Zealand before losing to France in the semifinals.\n\nFor Argentina, a grand final loss to France in Madrid was a setback after it topped the league stage of the world series, winning three of the seven stops.\n\nFor the Olympic tournament, Argentina is grouped with Australia, Samoa and Kenya in Pool B. No. 2-ranked Ireland, Tokyo silver medalist New Zealand, Rio bronze medalist South Africa and Japan are in a tough Pool A. Uruguay joins France, Fiji and the U.S. in Pool C.\n\nThe top two teams in each group and the two best third-place teams advance to the quarterfinals, meaning two-thirds of the 12 starters are still in medal contention when the knockout phase starts.\n\nThat's the stage where the Fijians have come into their own at the two previous Olympics.\n\nJerry Tuwai has been integral in Fiji's first two Olympic runs and the 35-year-old playmaker was recalled by Kolinisau two months ago after almost a year out of the team.\n\nA two-time Olympic champion, Sevens World Cup winner and player of the decade, Tuwai has embraced Kolinisau's approach ahead of the Paris Games.\n\n\"Our style of play has been opened up and our teamwork and communication. Our decision making -- that's another thing that opened up, too,\" Tuwai said. \"After two Olympic gold medals, these boys have shown they always show up in very big tournaments.\n\n\"We have this It'll be the same on Day 2 when the French meet two-time Olympic champion Fiji, the most formidable force in rugby's condensed sevens format.\n\nThe U.S. men face France and Fiji on Wednesday, giving them a unique view of a pair of title favorites.\n\n\"When we get in that environment, besides maybe 14 players, give or take 50 friends and family coming in supporting us, the staff and the people watching on TV -- we know it's going to be us versus 69,000 people,\" U.S. captain Kevon Williams said of facing the French. \"We're OK with that, we've been preparing for that, we've honed in and said, 'It's just us.'\n\n\"All we'll see is the French jersey, so we'll be ready.\"\n\nFrance hosted the Rugby World Cup last year and the national team again failed to lift the title. It has been a finalist three times at the sport's biggest tournament.\n\nWith undisputed star of the 15-a-side game joining its ranks, France has peaked in the rugby sevens format in 2024. Dupont helped the French win a spot on the world series for the first time in 19 years, and then capped it with a victory in the series finale in Madrid.\n\nThe French evolution has coincided with an unusually lean season for Fiji.\n\nAlthough Fiji head coach Osea Kolinisau is confident the team's bid for an Olympic three-peat will overshadow the inconsistent world series run by the time the men's sevens medals are awarded Saturday.\n\n\"We plan to keep that legacy going,\" Kolinisau said. \"We can claim it solely.\"\n\nKolinisau led Fiji to its first ever Olympic gold medal as captain in 2016 at Rio de Janeiro, where rugby sevens was featured on the Olympic program for the first time.\n\nKolinisau was rushed into the coaching role earlier this year to resurrect Fiji's men's program, and he reinstated what he calls the \"Fijian way\" -- or instinct -- for sevens rugby: \"High tempo, high risk.\"\n\nIn the series finale, the Fijians posted wins over Ireland, South Africa and New Zealand before losing to France in the semifinals.\n\nFor Argentina, a grand final loss to France in Madrid was a setback after it topped the league stage of the world series, winning three of the seven stops.\n\nFor the Olympic tournament, Argentina is grouped with Australia, Samoa and Kenya in Pool B. No. 2-ranked Ireland, Tokyo silver medalist New Zealand, Rio bronze medalist South Africa and Japan are in a tough Pool A. Uruguay joins France, Fiji and the U.S. in Pool C.\n\nThe top two teams in each group and the two best third-place teams advance to the quarterfinals, meaning two-thirds of the 12 starters are still in medal contention when the knockout phase starts.\n\nThat's the stage where the Fijians have come into their own at the two previous Olympics.\n\nJerry Tuwai has been integral in Fiji's first two Olympic runs and the 35-year-old playmaker was recalled by Kolinisau two months ago after almost a year out of the team.\n\nA two-time Olympic champion, Sevens World Cup winner and player of the decade, Tuwai has embraced Kolinisau's approach ahead of the Paris Games.\n\n\"Our style of play has been opened up and our teamwork and communication. Our decision making -- that's another thing that opened up, too,\" Tuwai said. \"After two Olympic gold medals, these boys have shown they always show up in very big tournaments.\n\nCopyright \u00a9 2024 The Associated Press. {"uri": "8239699042", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "15:27:23", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T15:27:23Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T15:25:26Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7568627595901489, "url": "https://exbulletin.com/fashion/2800441/", "title": "Rugby 7s set to kick off Paris 2024 Olympic Games in style - ExBulletin", "body": "69,000 spectators expected at each session at the Stade de France, which hosted the final of the 2023 Rugby World Cup\n\nThe captains of the 12 men's and 12 women's teams gathered in the Olympic Village on Monday ahead of what promises to be the most competitive and highly anticipated rugby sevens event in history.\n\nAfter rugby sevens' debut in Rio 2016 and the Covid-affected Tokyo 2020 Games, the sport is set to reach maturity on the Olympic stage in its third edition in Paris in front of a record crowd at the iconic Stade de France.\n\nRugby sevens proved to be one of the most popular events of the Paris Games, with more than 550,000 fans expected at the Stade de France over the eight sessions of competition, and a global television audience of several million more.\n\nThe men's competition will take place on July 24, 25 and 27, when the first gold medal of the Games will be awarded to the men's rugby sevens champions. The equally anticipated women's tournament will take place from July 28 to 30.\n\nSEE POOLS, SCHEDULE AND TEAMS >>\n\nAustralia and Samoa will have the honour of kicking off the Olympic competition when they take to the pitch for the first match at 15:30 local time CET (GMT+2) on 24 July. Hosts and recent SVNS Grand Final winners France, inspired by global superstar Antoine Dupont, will kick off their campaign on the USA pitch at 16:30, followed by two-time Olympic champions Fiji who will take on debutants Uruguay at 17:00.\n\nIreland and Great Britain will kick off the women's tournament at 3.30pm on July 28, while defending champions New Zealand will face Challenger champions China and SVNS Grand Final champions Australia will take on South Africa.\n\nThe format of the competition sees all teams play three pool matches with eight teams qualifying for the quarter-finals in the evening session on the second day of competition, before the third day sees the semi-finals and medal matches, so important that Olympic dreams come true and are shattered.\n\nRugby sevens is set to be one of the highlights of Paris 2024, following the resounding success of the 2023 Rugby World Cup in France. All the action will take place at the Stade de France, which hosted the opening match and final of the 2023 Rugby World Cup.\n\nFiji have won both men's gold medals to date - Rio being their first ever Olympic medal - but five different nations have won the men's SVNS series since 2016, while Argentina were crowned winners of the 2024 SVNS league and France claimed the inaugural SVNS Grand Final title in Madrid last month, demonstrating the depth of competitiveness.\n\nAustralia and New Zealand have taken women's rugby sevens to new levels, each winning an Olympic gold medal, while France won silver at Tokyo 2020 and could pose a strong challenge on home soil alongside the United States and Canada, among others.\n\nAll six World Rugby regions are represented among the 24 teams that have secured their place in Paris via the HSBC SVNS Series, regional qualifying competitions and the World Rugby Sevens Repechage. Three teams are making their Olympic debuts: Uruguay and Samoa are competing in the men's competition for the first time, while Ireland are making their Olympic debut.\n\nRUGBY SEVENS MEDIA GUIDE >>\n\nWorld Rugby Chairman Sir Bill Beaumont said: \"We are expecting a landmark event as rugby sevens kicks off the Paris 2024 Olympic Games at the Stade de France on Wednesday.\"\n\nThe Paris Games are the crown jewel of the greatest rugby sevens season in history. The stage is set for what will be a spectacular celebration of our sport at its peak.\n\nOver six days of intense and exciting competition, the stars of rugby sevens will shine brightly in front of what promises to be a record crowd for rugby sevens at these open Games, bringing our sport, its values and the joy of the Olympic Games to record audiences around the world. Paris is ready. Rugby is ready. Let's kick off these Games in style!\n\nAur\u00e9lie Merle, Paris 2024 Executive Director of Sports, added: \"This will be a great day for rugby sevens, and it's also a great day for us at Paris 2024, with the start of the rugby and football competitions. This is our kick-off. The stage is set and what a stage!\"\n\nWe want this third appearance of rugby sevens at the Olympic Games to be an exceptional and large-scale showcase for an exciting sport and its unique fan culture. With Paris 2024, we hope to add another dimension to the famous party culture that rugby sevens is renowned for. This fits perfectly with our vision of making these Games a spectacular and popular celebration.\n\nFrance captain Paulin Riva said: \"We feel good and we are very happy that rugby is the first discipline. We want to get this medal. We have had an incredible season and we have a lot of confidence and experience against the big teams like Argentina, Fiji and New Zealand, so we feel good and we just want to get on the pitch on Wednesday. There will be a great atmosphere at the Stade de France and we are very happy to see that for rugby sevens.\"\n\nRegarding Antoine Dupont's impact, he added: \"We think Antoine is the best player in the world and when he is on the pitch we feel a lot of confidence and that is very good for the team.\"\n\nNew Zealand women's team co-captain Sarah Hirini said: \"I'm really happy to be back and competing at another top event. It's so special and feels like the first time with the energy and excitement around the Olympic Village and within our team.\"\n\nWe're going to try to do something that's never been done before, try to make history and enjoy the moment. I'm really proud that we're playing in front of a huge crowd, it's the most important thing we can achieve as a sevens sport. I was there for the Men's World Cup last year and being in that packed stadium is going to be electric.\n\nJerry Tuwai, a two-time Olympic champion and captain of the Fiji men's team, said: \"Our main goal is to come and defend our Olympic gold medal. I'm very happy to be back. I was very emotional when I was left out of some of the events in the series, but I'm really happy to be here and aim for another gold medal.\"\n\nIt will be a great atmosphere and the pressure from the public will be on us so that we can play against France. Dupont is a very good player who influences people and makes the other players around him vibrate. He has my respect, like everyone else.\n\nAustralian women's captain Charlotte Caslick said: \"We're really excited. After a great camp in Montpellier and a great end to the sevens season, we're finally here and we can't wait to get started. We played really well but we also felt we had a lot of work to do, so we came home and did just that, working really hard to prepare.\"\n\nIt's really special to have our family and friends at the Stade de France and to be able to share our experience with them. We've been practicing ways to communicate with each other despite the noise of the crowd on the pitch, which is a good thing. Even being at the 2023 Rugby World Cup in that crowd last year was already incredible.\n\nAll teams will be competing for gold, but we have the legend Sharni Smale and we would like to give her a fairytale ending in addition to winning gold. We all want to win, of course, but we have that extra motivation!\n\nIreland captain Harry McNulty said: \"It's been really nice to settle into the Olympic Village. Everyone is relaxed and calm, enjoying these special moments and we can't wait to get going. Everyone can beat everyone and my ambition is to lead the team to a confident and competitive performance.\"\n\nIt's great that we're getting the Games off to a flying start and I think it's what the sport needs. We've got such an incredible sport that reaches all over the world and rugby sevens is so exciting and thrilling that we can't wait to get started.\n\nU.S. women's team captain Naya Taper said: \"Having this many fans in the stadium is both exciting and a little scary, at least for me. Tokyo 2020 was great, but we didn't have fans in the stands to cheer us on or boo us, so I'm preparing for that excitement. We've been preparing and we're really looking forward to getting started.\"\n\nWe are very pleased with what we were able to accomplish last season, but we know that the past is the past and the present is the present. We come here with the lessons and confidence we gained from last season, and we are taking that into this tournament.\n\nWe won't be the only ones and no one will give us an easy game, but we come here to make our friends and family proud and stand on this podium with a gold medal, not a silver medal, not a bronze medal, but a gold medal.\n\nIt's really inspiring to play on such a big platform. It fits our philosophy that women can be an inspiration to everyone watching, young boys and girls, fans and new audiences, by being someone they want to follow and be like and trying to be a role "Iconic French rugby star Antoine Dupont kicks off Olympic action at the Paris Games on Wednesday in a move that could not have been better scripted.\n\nRugby sevens will be held from July 24-30, with successful switch to the abbreviated game.\n\nHis absence from last season's Six Nations did not sit right with many France fans, still in shock at the team's quarter-final exit from the Rugby World Cup on French soil.\n\nBut for all the criticism, his absence, and Olympic presence, has been two years in the making.\n\nWorld Rugby boss Alan Gilpin said the inclusion of Dupont in the Olympics was essential to keep growing the sport.\n\n\"The Dupont impact is incredible,\" Gilpin said. \"It's provided a profile that we need to keep building.\"\n\nDupont's impact as a player in sevens has been {"uri": "8240170234", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "21:53:00", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T21:53:00Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T21:52:14Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7490196228027344, "url": "https://pina.com.fj/2024/07/24/rugby-sevens-set-to-kick-off-olympic-games-paris-2024-in-style/", "title": "0", "body": "Captains from the 12 men's and 12 women's teams gathered at the Olympic Village on Monday ahead of what promises to be the most hotly-contested and highly-anticipated rugby sevens event in history.\n\nFollowing rugby sevens' debut at Rio 2016 and the Covid affected Tokyo 2020 Games, the sport is set to 'come of age' on the Olympic stage at its third edition in Paris in front of a record breaking crowd at the iconic Stade de France.\n\nRugby Sevens has proven to be one of the highest demand events in the Paris Games with a more than 550,000 fans expected to fill Stade de France across the eight competition sessions, and a worldwide television audience of many millions more.\n\nThe men's competition will take place on 24, 25 and 27 July, when the first team sport gold medal of the Games will be awarded to the men's rugby sevens champions. The equally highly anticipated women's tournament follows on 28-30 July.\n\nAustralia and Samoa will have the honour of kicking off the Olympic competition as they take to the field for the first match at 15:30 local time CET (GMT+2) on 24 July. Hosts and recent SVNS Grand Final champions France inspired by global superstar Antoine Dupont will get their campaign under away the USA at 16:30 followed by double Olympic champions Fiji who face debutants Uruguay at 17:00.\n\nIreland and Great Britain will get play under way in the women's tournament at 15:30 on 28 July, while reigning champions New Zealand play Challenger champions China and SVNS Grand Final champions Australia kick off against South Africa.\n\nThe competition format sees all teams play three pool matches with eight teams qualifying for the quarter-finals in the evening session of the second day of competition, before the third day sees the semi-finals and the all-important medal matches as Olympic dreams are realised and broken.\n\nRugby sevens is expected to be one of the highlights of Paris 2024, following the resounding success of Rugby World Cup 2023 in France. All the action will take place at Stade de France, which was the venue for the opening match and final of Rugby World Cup 2023.\n\nFiji have famously won both men's gold medals to date - Rio being their first ever Olympic medal - but five different nations have won the men's SVNS Series since 2016, while Argentina were crowned SVNS 2024 league winners and France claimed the inaugural SVNS Grand Final title in Madrid last month, demonstrating the depth of competitiveness.\n\nAustralia and New Zealand have lifted the women's sevens game to new levels, winning one Olympic gold each, while France took silver at Tokyo 2020 and could provide a strong challenge on home soil, along with the likes of the USA and Canada among others.\n\nAll six World Rugby regions are represented among the 24 teams who secured their spots in Paris via the HSBC SVNS Series, regional qualification competitions and the World Rugby Sevens Repechage. There are three Olympic debutants with Uruguay and Samoa competing for the first time in the men's competition while Ireland's women make their first Olympic appearance.\n\nWorld Rugby Chairman Sir Bill Beaumont said: \"We anticipate a 'coming of age' event as rugby sevens kicks off the Paris 2024 Olympic Games at Stade de France on Wednesday.\n\n\"The Paris Games is the jewel in the crown of the biggest-ever sevens season. The stage is set for what will be a spectacular celebration of our sport at its breathtaking best.\n\n\"Over six days of highly competitive and compelling action, the stars of sevens will shine brightly in front of what promises to be a record crowd for Sevens at these 'Games wide open', taking our sport, its values and the joy of the Olympic Games to record audiences around the world. Paris is ready. Rugby is ready. Let's kick these Games off in style!\"\n\nParis 2024 Executive Sports Director Aurelie Merle added: \"It is going to be a big day for Rugby Sevens, and it's also a big day for us at Paris 2024, with the start of competitions in both rugby and football. It is our 'kick-off'. The stage is set - and what a stage!\n\n\"We want to make sure this third appearance of Rugby Sevens at the Olympic Games is an exceptional and high-profile showcase of a thrilling sport and its unique fan culture. With Paris 2024, we are hoping to add another dimension to the famous party culture that Rugby Sevens is known for. It's a perfect fit with our vision to make these Games a spectacular and popular celebration.\"\n\nFrance men's captain Paulin Riva said : \"We feel good and we are very excited that rugby is the first discipline. We want to catch this medal. We have had an amazing season and we have a lot of confidence and experience against the big teams like Argentina, Fiji and New Zealand so we feel good and we just want to get on to the field on Wednesday. It will be a big atmosphere in Stade de France and we are very happy to see this for rugby sevens.\"\n\nOn Antoine Dupont's impact he added: \"We think Antoine is the best player in the world and when he is on the pitch we feel a lot of confidence and it's very good for the team.\"\n\nNew Zealand women's co-captain Sarah Hirini said: \"I'm really happy to be back and at another pinnacle event. It is so special and it feels just like the first time with the energy and excitement around the Olympic Village and within our team.\n\n\"We're going to try and do something that's never been done before, trying to create history while enjoying the moment. I'm really proud that we will be playing in front of huge crowds, that's the most important thing that we can achieve as a sport for the sevens. I was here for the men's World Cup last year and being in that packed stadium is going to be electric.\"\n\nDouble Olympic champion and Fiji men's captain Jerry Tuwai said : \"The main goal for us is to come and defend our Olympic gold. I'm very happy to be back. It was emotional for me when I was left out for some Series events but I'm really happy to be here and going for another gold medal.\"\n\n\"It will be a great atmosphere and the pressure from the crowd will be on us to deliver when we play against France. Dupont is a very good player that influences people and makes other players around him tick and he has my respect, just the same as everyone else.\"\n\nAustralia women's captain Charlotte Caslick said: \"We are very excited. After a great camp in Montpellier and a great end of the sevens season, we are finally here and can't wait to begin. We have been playing very well but also felt we had a lot to work to do so we went home and did just that, working really hard to get ready.\n\n\"It is so special to have our family and friends in Stade de France and having the ability to share our experience with them. We have been practicing ways to be able to communicate between each other despite the crowd noise on the field, which is good. Even being part of Rugby World Cup 2023 in that crowd last year was already amazing.\n\n\"All the teams will be going for gold, but we have got the legend Sharni Smale and we would love to send her off with a fairytale finish as well as winning the gold. We obviously all want to win but have this extra motivation!\"\n\nIreland men's captain Harry McNulty said: \"It's been really nice to settle in to the Olympic Village. Everyone is feeling relaxed and calm, enjoying these special moments and we can't wait to kick off. Everyone can beat everyone and my ambition is to lead the squad to a confident performance and be competitive.\n\n\"It's amazing that we are kicking off the Games and I think it's what the sport needs. We have such an amazing sport that reaches all the way around the world and sevens is so exciting with many thrills and we can't wait to get started.\n\nUSA women's captain, Naya Taper said: \"Having so many fans in the stadium is both exciting and somehow scary, at least for me. Tokyo 2020 was great but we didn't have the fans in the stands cheering or booing for us so I'm getting ready for that stimulation. We have been preparing and are definitely looking forward to begin.\n\n\"We are very happy with what we have been able to achieve last season but we know the past is the past and the present is the present. We are coming here with the learning and the confidence we gained from last season, bringing it to this tournament.\n\n\"Bearing in mind we won't be the only one and nobody will give us an easy game but we are coming out here to make our friends and family proud and get on that podium with a gold medal, not a silver, not a bronze, but a gold medal.\n\n\"It is really inspiring to be playing on such a big platform. (Photo By Stephen McCarthy/Sportsfile via Getty Images)\n\nYes, rugby is an Olympic sport. Not in the full 15-a-side version of the game but in the shortened, exciting format of rugby sevens.\n\nRugby Sevens was introduced to the Olympics Games at Rio 2016. Fiji men won the nation's first-ever gold medal - men's or women's - by beating Team GB, who took silver. South Africa secured bronze over Japan. Australia won gold in the women's event while New Zealand took silver and Canada took bronze.\n\nIn Tokyo 2020, Fiji men defended their title with New Zealand taking silver and Argentina taking bronze. New Zealand women earned gold, France took silver and Fiji took bronze.\n\nInterestingly, the 15-a-side union format of the game was an Olympic sport but was last featured 100 years ago. A men's event debuted at the 1900 Games, also in Paris, with home side France taking gold. The last 15s medal was awarded at the 1924 Game, again in Paris, with the USA taking the title.\n\nThis means that the defending Olympic champions in rugby union are technically the USA.\n\nRugby at the Paris 2024 Olympics: Need to know\n\nRugby Sevens captains at Paris 2024 Olympic Games (Getty Images)\n\nParis 2024 will see 12 men's and 12 women's teams compete in Rugby Sevens for gold. There will then be a quarter final, semis, final and third-place bronze medal play-off.\n\nThe first men's game will be Australia vs Samoa at 14:30 BST on Wednesday 24th while the women's competition begins with Ireland vs Team GB at 14:30 BST on Sunday 28th.\n\nThe men's bronze medal match takes place at 18:00 BST on Saturday 27th July, followed by the gold medal match at 18:45 BST - the first medals to be awarded at Paris 2024. The women's medals matches will then take place at the same time on Tuesday 30th July.\n\nRugby at the Paris 2024 Olympics: Teams\n\nThere will be 12 nations taking part in both the men's and women's competition. It'll be the same on Day 2 when the French meet two-time Olympic champion Fiji, the most formidable force in rugby's condensed sevens format.\n\nThe U.S. men face France and Fiji on Wednesday, giving them a unique view of a pair of title favorites.\n\n\"When we get in that environment, besides maybe 14 players, give or take 50 friends and family coming in supporting us, the staff and the people watching on TV -- we know it's going to be us versus 69,000 people,\" U.S. captain Kevon Williams said of facing the French. \"We're OK with that, we've been preparing for that, we've honed in and said, 'It's just us.'\n\n\"All we'll see is the French jersey, so we'll be ready.\"\n\nFrance hosted the Rugby World Cup last year and the national team again failed to lift the title. It has been a finalist three times at the sport's biggest tournament.\n\nWith undisputed star of the 15-a-side game joining its ranks, France has peaked in the rugby sevens format in 2024. Dupont helped the French win a spot on the world series for the first time in 19 years, and then capped it with a victory in the series finale in Madrid.\n\nThe French evolution has coincided with an unusually lean season for Fiji.\n\nAlthough Fiji head coach Osea Kolinisau is confident the team's bid for an Olympic three-peat will overshadow the inconsistent world series run by the time the men's sevens medals are awarded Saturday.\n\n\"We plan to keep that legacy going,\" Kolinisau said. \"We can claim it solely.\"\n\nKolinisau led Fiji to its first ever Olympic gold medal as captain in 2016 at Rio de Janeiro, where rugby sevens was featured on the Olympic program for the first time.\n\nKolinisau was rushed into the coaching role earlier this year to resurrect Fiji's men's program, and he reinstated what he calls the \"Fijian way\" -- or instinct -- for sevens rugby: \"High tempo, high risk.\"\n\nIn the series finale, the Fijians posted wins over Ireland, South Africa and New Zealand before losing to France in the semifinals.\n\nFor Argentina, a grand final loss to France in Madrid was a setback after it topped the league stage of the world series, winning three of the seven stops.\n\nFor the Olympic tournament, Argentina is grouped with Australia, Samoa and Kenya in Pool B. No. 2-ranked Ireland, Tokyo silver medalist New Zealand, Rio bronze medalist South Africa and Japan are in a tough Pool A. Uruguay joins France, Fiji and the U.S. in Pool C.\n\nThe top two teams in each group and the two best third-place teams advance to the quarterfinals, meaning two-thirds of the 12 starters are still in medal contention when the knockout phase starts.\n\nThat's the stage where the Fijians have come into their own at the two previous Olympics.\n\nJerry Tuwai has been integral in Fiji's first two Olympic runs and the 35-year-old playmaker was recalled by Kolinisau two months ago after almost a year out of the team.\n\nA two-time Olympic champion, Sevens World Cup winner and player of the decade, Tuwai has embraced Kolinisau's approach ahead of the Paris Games.\n\n\"Our style of play has been opened up and our teamwork and communication. Our decision making -- that's another thing that opened up, too,\" Tuwai said. \"After two Olympic gold medals, these boys have shown they always show up in very big tournaments.\n\n\"We have this {"uri": "2024-07-431119224", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "16:07:03", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T16:07:03Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T16:06:53Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6980392336845398, "url": "https://www.world.rugby/news/946163?lang=en", "title": "Rugby Sevens set to kick-off Olympic Games Paris 2024 in style", "body": "Rugby Sevens is set to come of age on the Olympic stage when the sport has the honour of kicking off the Olympic Games Paris 2024 in front of a capacity crowd of 69,000 fans at Stade de France on Wednesday\n\nCaptains from the 12 men's and 12 women's teams gathered at the Olympic Village on Monday ahead of what promises to be the most hotly-contested and highly-anticipated rugby sevens event in history.\n\nFollowing rugby sevens' debut at Rio 2016 and the Covid affected Tokyo 2020 Games, the sport is set to 'come of age' on the Olympic stage at its third edition in Paris in front of a record breaking crowd at the iconic Stade de France.\n\nRugby Sevens has proven to be one of the highest demand events in the Paris Games with a more than 550,000 fans expected to fill Stade de France across the eight competition sessions, and a worldwide television audience of many millions more.\n\nThe men's competition will take place on 24, 25 and 27 July, when the first team sport gold medal of the Games will be awarded to the men's rugby sevens champions. The equally highly anticipated women's tournament follows on 28-30 July.\n\nVIEW POOLS, SCHEDULE AND SQUADS >>\n\nAustralia and Samoa will have the honour of kicking off the Olympic competition as they take to the field for the first match at 15:30 local time CET (GMT+2) on 24 July. Hosts and recent SVNS Grand Final champions France inspired by global superstar Antoine Dupont will get their campaign under away the USA at 16:30 followed by double Olympic champions Fiji who face debutants Uruguay at 17:00.\n\nIreland and Great Britain will get play under way in the women's tournament at 15:30 on 28 July, while reigning champions New Zealand play Challenger champions China and SVNS Grand Final champions Australia kick off against South Africa.\n\nThe competition format sees all teams play three pool matches with eight teams qualifying for the quarter-finals in the evening session of the second day of competition, before the third day sees the semi-finals and the all-important medal matches as Olympic dreams are realised and broken.\n\nRugby sevens is expected to be one of the highlights of Paris 2024, following the resounding success of Rugby World Cup 2023 in France. All the action will take place at Stade de France, which was the venue for the opening match and final of Rugby World Cup 2023.\n\nFiji have famously won both men's gold medals to date - Rio being their first ever Olympic medal - but five different nations have won the men's SVNS Series since 2016, while Argentina were crowned SVNS 2024 league winners and France claimed the inaugural SVNS Grand Final title in Madrid last month, demonstrating the depth of competitiveness.\n\nAustralia and New Zealand have lifted the women's sevens game to new levels, winning one Olympic gold each, while France took silver at Tokyo 2020 and could provide a strong challenge on home soil, along with the likes of the USA and Canada among others.\n\nAll six World Rugby regions are represented among the 24 teams who secured their spots in Paris via the HSBC SVNS Series, regional qualification competitions and the World Rugby Sevens Repechage. There are three Olympic debutants with Uruguay and Samoa competing for the first time in the men's competition while Ireland's women make their first Olympic appearance.\n\nRUGBY SEVENS MEDIA GUIDE >>\n\nWorld Rugby Chairman Sir Bill Beaumont said: \"We anticipate a 'coming of age' event as rugby sevens kicks off the Paris 2024 Olympic Games at Stade de France on Wednesday.\n\n\"The Paris Games is the jewel in the crown of the biggest-ever sevens season. The stage is set for what will be a spectacular celebration of our sport at its breathtaking best.\n\n\"Over six days of highly competitive and compelling action, the stars of sevens will shine brightly in front of what promises to be a record crowd for Sevens at these 'Games wide open', taking our sport, its values and the joy of the Olympic Games to record audiences around the world. Paris is ready. Rugby is ready. Let's kick these Games off in style!\"\n\nParis 2024 Executive Sports Director Aurelie Merle added: \"It is going to be a big day for Rugby Sevens, and it's also a big day for us at Paris 2024, with the start of competitions in both rugby and football. It is our 'kick-off'. The stage is set - and what a stage!\n\n\"We want to make sure this third appearance of Rugby Sevens at the Olympic Games is an exceptional and high-profile showcase of a thrilling sport and its unique fan culture. With Paris 2024, we are hoping to add another dimension to the famous party culture that Rugby Sevens is known for. It's a perfect fit with our vision to make these Games a spectacular and popular celebration.\"\n\nFrance men's captain Paulin Riva said : \"We feel good and we are very excited that rugby is the first discipline. We want to catch this medal. We have had an amazing season and we have a lot of confidence and experience against the big teams like Argentina, Fiji and New Zealand so we feel good and we just want to get on to the field on Wednesday. It will be a big atmosphere in Stade de France and we are very happy to see this for rugby sevens.\"\n\nOn Antoine Dupont's impact he added: \"We think Antoine is the best player in the world and when he is on the pitch we feel a lot of confidence and it's very good for the team.\"\n\nNew Zealand women's co-captain Sarah Hirini said: \"I'm really happy to be back and at another pinnacle event. It is so special and it feels just like the first time with the energy and excitement around the Olympic Village and within our team.\n\n\"We're going to try and do something that's never been done before, trying to create history while enjoying the moment. I'm really proud that we will be playing in front of huge crowds, that's the most important thing that we can achieve as a sport for the sevens. I was here for the men's World Cup last year and being in that packed stadium is going to be electric.\"\n\nDouble Olympic champion and Fiji men's captain Jerry Tuwai said : \"The main goal for us is to come and defend our Olympic gold. I'm very happy to be back. It was emotional for me when I was left out for some Series events but I'm really happy to be here and going for another gold medal.\"\n\n\"It will be a great atmosphere and the pressure from the crowd will be on us to deliver when we play against France. Dupont is a very good player that influences people and makes other players around him tick and he has my respect, just the same as everyone else.\"\n\nAustralia women's captain Charlotte Caslick said: \"We are very excited. After a great camp in Montpellier and a great end of the sevens season, we are finally here and can't wait to begin. We have been playing very well but also felt we had a lot to work to do so we went home and did just that, working really hard to get ready.\n\n\"It is so special to have our family and friends in Stade de France and having the ability to share our experience with them. We have been practicing ways to be able to communicate between each other despite the crowd noise on the field, which is good. Even being part of Rugby World Cup 2023 in that crowd last year was already amazing.\n\n\"All the teams will be going for gold, but we have got the legend Sharni Smale and we would love to send her off with a fairytale finish as well as winning the gold. We obviously all want to win but have this extra motivation!\"\n\nIreland men's captain Harry McNulty said: \"It's been really nice to settle in to the Olympic Village. Everyone is feeling relaxed and calm, enjoying these special moments and we can't wait to kick off. Everyone can beat everyone and my ambition is to lead the squad to a confident performance and be competitive.\n\n\"It's amazing that we are kicking off the Games and I think it's what the sport needs. We have such an amazing sport that reaches all the way around the world and sevens is so exciting with many thrills and we can't wait to get started.\n\nUSA women's captain, Naya Taper said: \"Having so many fans in the stadium is both exciting and somehow scary, at least for me. Tokyo 2020 was great but we didn't have the fans in the stands cheering or booing for us so I'm getting ready for that stimulation. We have been preparing and are definitely looking forward to begin.\n\n\"We are very happy with what we have been able to achieve last season but we know the past is the past and the present is the present. We are coming here with the learning and the confidence we gained from last season, bringing it to this tournament.\n\n\"Bearing in mind we won't be the only one and nobody will give us an easy game but we are coming out here to make our friends and family proud and get on that podium with a gold medal, not a silver, not a bronze, but a gold medal.\n\n\"It is really inspiring to be playing on such a big platform. It relates to our philosophy that women can be a source of inspiration for anyone watching, young boys and young girls, fans and new publics, being somebody they want to follow behind and strive to be {"uri": "8240219153", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "22:47:52", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T22:47:52Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T22:45:43Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.658823549747467, "url": "https://kuwaittimes.com/article/16998/sports/other-sports/dupont-guarantees-spotlight-firmly-on-rugby-sevens-clerc/", "title": "Dupont guarantees spotlight firmly on rugby sevens: Clerc", "body": "PARIS: French star Antoine Dupont has the capability of drawing in a new generation of fans while also putting rugby sevens firmly in the spotlight, according to ex-France winger Vincent Clerc. Dupont took a gamble of missing the Six Nations to make the French Olympic team, a move many traditionalists criticized.\n\nBut the scrum-half went on to help France to two wins on the World Rugby Sevens Series, including victory in the Madrid finals. In between, he skippered his club Toulouse to Top 14 and Champions Cup glory in the 15-a-side code.\n\n\"Antoine is an exceptional player and there's currently no equivalent in terms of putting in performances,\" Clerc said Tuesday, a day ahead of the start of the men's Olympic rugby sevens tournament at the Stade de France.\n\n\"He will attract a new, different audience. Sevens has long suffered from the 15-a-side calendar, where it has been very tricky for players to play both codes.\" Clerc, capped 67 times by France, added: \"Rugby sevens has improved some of Antoine's skills, even though they were already at a very high level.\n\n\"And rugby sevens will benefit from Antoine's image, his desire to highlight rugby sevens and to show that winning an Olympic medal in rugby is worth the same as the Top 14 title or Champions Cup crown.\"\n\nTransition between sevens and 15s\n\nWorld Rugby Chief Executive Alan Gilpin said Dupont's apparent ease at transitioning between 15-a-side rugby and the abbreviated game was unmatched, but should also be encouraged. \"It should be possible in the big global-stage moments in sevens and 15s that the players can try and play in both,\" Gilpin said.\n\n\"What Antoine Dupont is doing is utterly incredible. To make that transition not just once in a season, but to do it back and forth, from being player of the match in the Champions Cup one weekend to then leading France to victory in the sevens grand finale in Madrid, was incredible.\n\n\"And again, I think it inspires more players to want to do that.\" Clerc agreed that Dupont's transition had shown the way. \"You can see that it is possible for 15s players to play sevens,\" he said. \"It was considered a sport that was too specific, too tough to transition, but with precise management and intelligent coaching, it's possible.\"\n\nFanny Horta, who captained the French women's team to silver in Tokyo, said Dupont \"has an aura on the pitch, he's someone who gives the impression of being calm\".\n\n\"He gives confidence to the France team. His teammates have raised their own game since he joined the squad.\" Dupont's presence has certainly boosted the rugby competition, with a 69,000 sell-out crowd for each of the three days of action. {"uri": "2024-07-431079610", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "15:28:38", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T15:28:38Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T14:31:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6509804129600525, "url": "https://www.insidethegames.biz/articles/1146946/rugby-sevens-paris-all-you-need-to-know", "title": "Rugby sevens in Paris: All you need to know", "body": "Rugby sevens is a condensed version of rugby union, featuring seven players on each team rather than the usual fifteen. The game is played on a standard rugby field, but matches are significantly shorter, with each half lasting only seven minutes. This results in high-intensity action and often high-scoring games. The reduced number of players and the abbreviated match time emphasise speed, agility, and strategic play, making rugby sevens a thrilling spectacle.\n\nThe objective of rugby sevens is the same as in traditional rugby: to score points by carrying the ball over the opponent's try line or by kicking it between the goalposts. A try, worth five points, is scored when a player grounds the ball in the in-goal area. After a try, the scoring team has the opportunity to add two more points with a conversion kick. Additionally, teams can score points through penalty goals and drop goals, each worth three points.\n\nThe structure of the Olympic rugby sevens tournament is designed to showcase the sport's rapid pace and unpredictability. Teams are divided into pools, and each team plays every other team in their pool. The top teams from each pool, along with the best-performing runners-up, advance to the knockout stages. This format ensures that every match is crucial, as teams vie for a spot in the quarterfinals, semifinals, and ultimately, the final.\n\nRugby sevens made its Olympic debut at the 2016 Rio Games, marking the return of rugby to the Olympics after a 92-year absence. Rugby union had previously been included in four Olympic Games from 1900 to 1924. The reintroduction of rugby, in its sevens format, was met with widespread enthusiasm, and the tournament in Rio was a resounding success. Fiji's men's team and Australia's women's team made history by winning the first-ever Olympic gold medals in rugby sevens.\n\nThe inclusion of rugby sevens, which will be played at the Stade de France, has had a significant impact on the sport's global popularity. The fast-paced, entertaining nature of sevens has attracted new fans and participants, helping to grow rugby's presence worldwide. Moreover, the Olympic platform has provided a stage for emerging rugby nations to compete against established powerhouses, contributing to the sport's development.\n\nIn preparation for the Olympics, teams undergo rigorous training and participate in the World Rugby Sevens Series, an annual series of international tournaments. This series allows teams to hone their skills, develop strategies, and gain valuable experience against top-tier competition. The World Rugby Sevens Series also serves as a qualifying pathway for the Olympics, with teams earning points based on their performance throughout the season.\n\nAs rugby sevens continues to evolve, its presence at the Olympics remains a highlight for both players and fans. The sport's blend of athleticism, strategy, and excitement makes it a perfect fit for the Olympic stage. With each edition of the Games, rugby sevens further cements its status as a must-watch event, showcasing the best of rugby's thrilling and dynamic nature. Sevens has long suffered from the 15-a-side calendar, where it has been very tricky for players to play both codes.\"\n\nClerc, capped 67 times by France, added: \"Rugby sevens has improved some of Antoine's skills, even though they were already at a very high level.\n\n\"And rugby sevens will benefit from Antoine's image, his desire to highlight rugby sevens and to show that winning an Olympic medal in rugby is worth the same as the Top 14 title or Champions Cup crown.\"\n\nTransition between sevens and 15s\n\nWorld Rugby Chief Executive Alan Gilpin said Dupont's apparent ease at transitioning between 15-a-side rugby and the abbreviated game was unmatched, but should also be encouraged.\n\n\"It should be possible in the big global-stage moments in sevens and 15s that the players can try and play in both,\" Gilpin said.\n\n\"What Antoine Dupont is doing is utterly incredible. To make that transition not just once in a season, but to do it back and forth, from being player of the match in the Champions Cup one weekend to then leading France to victory in the sevens grand finale in Madrid, was incredible.\n\n\"And again, I think it inspires more players to want to do that.\"\n\nClerc agreed that Dupont's transition had shown the way.\n\n\"You can see that it is possible for 15s players to play sevens,\" he said.\n\n\"It was considered a sport that was too specific, too tough to transition, but with precise management and intelligent coaching, it's possible.\"\n\nFanny Horta, who captained the French women's team to silver in Tokyo, said Dupont \"has an aura on the pitch, he's someone who gives the impression of being calm\".\n\n\"He gives confidence to the France team. His teammates have raised their own game since he joined the squad.\"\n\nDupont's presence has certainly boosted the rugby competition, with a 69,000 sell-out crowd for each of the three days of action.\n\n\"Antoine is an exceptional player,\" added Clerc, who was part of the French sevens team that won a series leg in Paris in 2005.\n\n\"He might only play a couple of minutes, but he's capable of turning a match on its head. {"uri": "8240377319", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "02:00:23", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T02:00:23Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T01:57:11Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6117647290229797, "url": "https://www.rnz.co.nz/news/olympics-2024/523001/olympics-rugby-sevens-ranking-each-team-s-chances-of-gold", "title": "Olympics rugby sevens: Ranking each team's chances of gold", "body": "The speed, skill and flair on display in rugby sevens makes it an ideal Olympic sport. The Paris games should be no exception, especially given France's own great rugby tradition.\n\nWhile the conventional 15-a-side game has only ever featured at four Olympics (1900, 1908, 1920 and 1924), sevens debuted at the Rio de Janeiro games in 2016, capturing fans with its festive atmosphere and fast-running athleticism.\n\nAnd although the traditionally strong rugby-playing nations tend to dominate the sevens version, it also allows the \"minnows\" to compete and sometimes surprise the heavyweights.\n\nSo, which teams are favourites to win medals in Paris? To answer this we've used a suite of statistical models known as Rugby Vision. This modelling system has outperformed bookmakers when forecasting outcomes for Rugby World Cup games.\n\nRugby Vision has three components:\n\nBy examining the number of times in the 10,000 simulations that each team \"wins\" the tournament, we can calculate the probability of each team winning the gold medal. Both the men's and women's tournaments have been analysed this way.\n\nMedal probabilities for each of the 12 qualified teams in the men's tournament, which begins on 24 July, are displayed below.\n\nArgentina, which dominated the 2023-24 SVNS, is favourite to win (28.1 percent) and has a 60.4 percent chance of earning any medal. France, which has home advantage and won the 2023-24 SVNS grand final, is second favourite (22.3 percent), followed by Ireland (12.5. percent), which was a consistent performer in the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nTraditional sevens powerhouses Fiji (which won gold at the two previous Olympics) and New Zealand are fourth and fifth favourites respectively. This reflects mixed performances by both teams at the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nThe women's tournament kicks off on 28 July, with New Zealand (34.8 percent) and Australia (31.1 percent) most likely to win gold. Between them, these two teams won seven of the eight 2023-24 SVNS tournaments.\n\nFrance is third favourite (25.9 percent), with the US (4.0 percent) and Canada (2.2 percent) rounding out the five most likely winners.\n\nAlthough New Zealand has a higher chance than Australia of winning gold, Australia has a higher chance of winning any medal. This is because the algorithm rates Australia a (slightly) stronger team than New Zealand - but New Zealand is expected to have an easier semi-final opponent.\n\nOf course, the algorithm's favourite does not always win. At the 2023 Rugby World Cup, for example, Rugby Vision ranked New Zealand likeliest to win, with South Africa second. South Africa beat New Zealand in the final.\n\nThe same uncertainty applies at the Olympic sevens. While Argentina is favourite to win the men's tournament, there is still a 72 percent chance another team will take home the gold. Our algorithm uses 10,000 simulations to rank the teams", "body": "Niven Winchester, Professor of Economics, Auckland University of Technology\n\nThe speed, skill and flair on display in rugby sevens makes it an ideal Olympic sport. The Paris games should be no exception, especially given France's own great rugby tradition.\n\nWhile the conventional 15-a-side game has only ever featured at four Olympics (1900, 1908, 1920 and 1924), sevens debuted at the Rio de Janeiro games in 2016, capturing fans with its festive atmosphere and fast-running athleticism.\n\nAnd although the traditionally strong rugby-playing nations tend to dominate the sevens version, it also allows the \"minnows\" to compete and sometimes surprise the heavyweights.\n\nSo, which teams are favourites to win medals in Paris? To answer this we've used a suite of statistical models known as Rugby Vision. This modelling system has outperformed bookmakers when forecasting outcomes for Rugby World Cup games.\n\nRugby Vision has three components:\n\nBy examining the number of times in the 10,000 simulations that each team \"wins\" the tournament, we can calculate the probability of each team winning the gold medal. Both the men's and women's tournaments have been analysed this way.\n\nMedal probabilities for each of the 12 qualified teams in the men's tournament, which begins on July 24, are displayed below.\n\nArgentina, which dominated the 2023-24 SVNS, is favourite to win (28.1%) and has a 60.4% chance of earning any medal. France, which has home advantage and won the 2023-24 SVNS grand final, is second favourite (22.3%), followed by Ireland (12.5.%), which was a consistent performer in the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nTraditional sevens powerhouses Fiji (which won gold at the two previous Olympics) and New Zealand are fourth and fifth favourites respectively. This reflects mixed performances by both teams at the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nThe women's tournament kicks off on July 28, with New Zealand (34.8%) and Australia (31.1%) most likely to win gold. Between them, these two teams won seven of the eight 2023-24 SVNS tournaments.\n\nFrance is third favourite (25.9%), with the USA (4.0%) and Canada (2.2%) rounding out the five most likely winners.\n\nAlthough New Zealand has a higher chance than Australia of winning gold, Australia has a higher chance of winning any medal. This is because the algorithm rates Australia a (slightly) stronger team than New Zealand - but New Zealand is expected to have an easier semi-final opponent.\n\nOf course, the algorithm's favourite does not always win. At the 2023 Rugby World Cup, for example, Rugby Vision ranked New Zealand likeliest to win, with South Africa second. South Africa beat New Zealand in the final.\n\nThe same uncertainty applies at the Olympic sevens. While Argentina is favourite to win the men's tournament, there is still a 72% chance another team will take home the gold. Upsets should be expected - that is why watching sport is so enthralling.\n\nThe author acknowledges the assistance of Jensen Fiskin, whose data collection contributed to the forecasts included in Fiji in the past two years.\n\nSamoa, under coach Muliagatele Brian Lima, are in Pool B.\n\nThey face Australia, Kenya and Argentina in pool play, opening the competition against the Aussies in the very first game on Thursday morning.\n\nFinishing in the bottom end of the HSBC Series this year saw them having to go through the play-off.\n\nThat did not finish well for them and they are now out Australia and Argentina on Thursday morning before meeting Kenya on Friday.\n\nMany are tipping host France, 2024 HSBC winner Argentina, New Zealand and Ireland as the top favourites to claim the men's title.\n\nSo, Fiji, even as defending champions, will go in as the underdog.\n\nFiii's mentor Kolinisau is no stranger to the Olympics.\n\nHe was captain in 2016 when they created history winning the first-ever Olympic sevens rugby gold medal - which was also Fiji's first at the Games.\n\nHe told FBC Sports they will focus on one game at a time.\n\nThat means their goal right now is The Japanese side suffered defeat to New Zealand in the other Pool A clash this afternoon.\n\nAlthough the Olympics opening ceremony is not until Friday, soccer and rugby sevens preliminary rounds got underway for logistical reasons in Paris and around the country.\n\nThe shorter but speedier rugby format allows teams to play more than one match a day and the medals in the men's and women's tournaments will be decided before the 81,000-capacity stadium hosts the athletics events from August 1st.\n\nScores of fans lined up outside the sun-kissed arena for the rugby sevens, the majority in blue to support the host nation.\n\n\"It's been excitement, emotions, impatience ... I've been looking forward to the start,\" said 44-year-old France fan Matthieu.\n\n\"We're at the heart of the biggest event that we've been waiting a long time to see.\"\n\nAnother France fan, Pauline from Toulouse, arrived with three kids in tow and there was no question who they were most keen to watch when they screamed, \"Antoine Dupont!\".\n\nThe 27-year-old is a former world player of the year in the fifteen-man format and made the switch to Sevens after last year's Rugby World Cup, immediately elevating France to title contenders with his versatility.\n\nThe loudest cheer of the day was reserved for when Dupont, who has mostly come on as an impact replacement, was announced in the starting lineup in the Pool C opener against the United States.\n\nThe crowd were treated to a thriller of a match with American Marcus Tupuola scoring a late try to lock up the scores at 12-12. Madison Hughes missed the conversion leaving the two teams to share the spoils.\n\n\"It was a huge atmosphere,\" Dupont said. \"It's not common for us to play in this kind of stadium, we have to embrace this atmosphere, to embrace this pressure, to play better in the next game.\"\n\nFiji are seeking a hat-trick of golds to underline their dominance in their national sport and they later went top of Pool C with a thumping 40-12 victory over Uruguay, who were no match for the speed and power of the Pacific islanders.\n\nEarlier, Australia kicked off their Pool B campaign with a 21-14 win over Samoa fired by two tries from veteran flyer Henry Hutchison.\n\nArgentina were roundly booed by the crowd when they took to the pitch for their Pool B match against Kenya in what was perhaps a spillover from the 2022 soccer World Cup final between France and the South Americans.\n\nSuch was their disdain for the men in powder blue-and-white, the crowd jeered even when Argentina scored their five tries while loudly cheering on every Kenya move.\n\nArgentina were unperturbed as they toyed with the African side and eased to a 31-12 victory.\n\nThe pool games continue in the evening {"uri": "2024-07-431441290", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "23:57:04", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T23:57:04Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T23:56:41Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5764706134796143, "url": "https://foreignaffairs.co.nz/2024/07/24/mil-evening-report-who-will-win-olympic-rugby-sevens-gold-our-algorithm-uses-10000-simulations-to-rank-the-teams/", "title": "MIL-Evening Report: Who will win Olympic rugby sevens gold? Our algorithm uses 10,000 simulations to rank the teams", "body": "Source: The Conversation (Au and NZ) - By Niven Winchester, Professor of Economics, Auckland University of Technology\n\nThe speed, skill and flair on display in rugby sevens makes it an ideal Olympic sport. The Paris games should be no exception, especially given France's own great rugby tradition.\n\nWhile the conventional 15-a-side game has only ever featured at four Olympics (1900, 1908, 1920 and 1924), sevens debuted at the Rio de Janeiro games in 2016, capturing fans with its festive atmosphere and fast-running athleticism.\n\nAnd although the traditionally strong rugby-playing nations tend to dominate the sevens version, it also allows the \"minnows\" to compete and sometimes surprise the heavyweights.\n\nSo, which teams are favourites to win medals in Paris? To answer this we've used a suite of statistical models known as Rugby Vision. This modelling system has outperformed bookmakers when forecasting outcomes for Rugby World Cup games.\n\nBy examining the number of times in the 10,000 simulations that each team \"wins\" the tournament, we can calculate the probability of each team winning the gold medal. Both the men's and women's tournaments have been analysed this way.\n\nArgentina lead the men's pack\n\nMedal probabilities for each of the 12 qualified teams in the men's tournament, which begins on July 24, are displayed below.\n\nArgentina, which dominated the 2023-24 SVNS, is favourite to win (28.1%) and has a 60.4% chance of earning any medal. France, which has home advantage and won the 2023-24 SVNS grand final, is second favourite (22.3%), followed by Ireland (12.5.%), which was a consistent performer in the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nTraditional sevens powerhouses Fiji (which won gold at the two previous Olympics) and New Zealand are fourth and fifth favourites respectively. This reflects mixed performances by both teams at the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nNZ versus Australia for the women's gold\n\nThe women's tournament kicks off on July 28, with New Zealand (34.8%) and Australia (31.1%) most likely to win gold. Between them, these two teams won seven of the eight 2023-24 SVNS tournaments.\n\nFrance is third favourite (25.9%), with the USA (4.0%) and Canada (2.2%) rounding out the five most likely winners.\n\nAlthough New Zealand has a higher chance than Australia of winning gold, Australia has a higher chance of winning any medal. This is because the algorithm rates Australia a (slightly) stronger team than New Zealand - but New Zealand is expected to have an easier semi-final opponent.\n\nOf course, the algorithm's favourite does not always win. At the 2023 Rugby World Cup, for example, Rugby Vision ranked New Zealand likeliest to win, with South Africa second. South Africa beat New Zealand in the final.\n\nThe same uncertainty applies at the Olympic sevens. While Argentina is favourite to win the men's tournament, there is still a 72% chance another team will take home the gold. Upsets should be expected - that is why watching sport is so enthralling.\n\nThe author acknowledges the assistance of Jensen Fiskin, whose data collection contributed to the forecasts included in this article.\n\nNiven Winchester does not work for, consult, own shares in or receive funding from any company or organisation that would benefit from this article, and has disclosed no relevant But the home crowd was stunned into silence just before the half-time whistle as US flyer Lucas Lacamp broke through the French defence for a long-range effort that earned his team a 7-5 lead at the break.\n\nFrance restored their advantage practically from the kick-off in the second half, Rayan Rebbadj powering over after a move that started with a clever Dupont offload. {"uri": "8240253813", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "23:33:11", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T23:33:11Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T23:28:36Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5568627715110779, "url": "https://www.miragenews.com/algorithm-predicts-olympic-rugby-sevens-gold-1281696/", "title": "Algorithm Predicts Olympic Rugby Sevens Gold Winner", "body": "The speed, skill and flair on display in rugby sevens makes it an ideal Olympic sport. The Paris games should be no exception, especially given France's own great rugby tradition.\n\nAuthor\n\nNiven Winchester\n\nProfessor of Economics, Auckland University of Technology\n\nWhile the conventional 15-a-side game has only ever featured at four Olympics (1900, 1908, 1920 and 1924), sevens debuted at the Rio de Janeiro games in 2016, capturing fans with its festive atmosphere and fast-running athleticism.\n\nAnd although the traditionally strong rugby-playing nations tend to dominate the sevens version, it also allows the \"minnows\" to compete and sometimes surprise the heavyweights.\n\nSo, which teams are favourites to win medals in Paris? To answer this we've used a suite of statistical models known as Rugby Vision. This modelling system has outperformed bookmakers when forecasting outcomes for Rugby World Cup games.\n\nHow the prediction model works\n\nRugby Vision has three components:\n\nan algorithm uses past game statistics to rate the strength of each sevens team, based on results from the 2023-24 SVNS international tournaments and other Olympic qualification rounds\n\nthe ratings (and home advantage for France) are then used to simulate the expected outcome of each game\n\nthe tournament is simulated 10,000 times to account for uncertainty around expected outcomes.\n\nBy examining the number of times in the 10,000 simulations that each team \"wins\" the tournament, we can calculate the probability of each team winning the gold medal. Both the men's and women's tournaments have been analysed this way.\n\nArgentina lead the men's pack\n\nMedal probabilities for each of the 12 qualified teams in the men's tournament, which begins on July 24, are displayed below.\n\nArgentina, which dominated the 2023-24 SVNS, is favourite to win (28.1%) and has a 60.4% chance of earning any medal. France, which has home advantage and won the 2023-24 SVNS grand final, is second favourite (22.3%), followed by Ireland (12.5.%), which was a consistent performer in the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nTraditional sevens powerhouses Fiji (which won gold at the two previous Olympics) and New Zealand are fourth and fifth favourites respectively. This reflects mixed performances by both teams at the 2023-24 SVNS.\n\nNZ versus Australia for the women's gold\n\nThe women's tournament kicks off on July 28, with New Zealand (34.8%) and Australia (31.1%) most likely to win gold. Between them, these two teams won seven of the eight 2023-24 SVNS tournaments.\n\nFrance is third favourite (25.9%), with the USA (4.0%) and Canada (2.2%) rounding out the five most likely winners.\n\nAlthough New Zealand has a higher chance than Australia of winning gold, Australia has a higher chance of winning any medal. This is because the algorithm rates Australia a (slightly) stronger team than New Zealand - but New Zealand is expected to have an easier semi-final opponent.\n\nOf course, the algorithm's favourite does not always win. At the 2023 Rugby World Cup, for example, Rugby Vision ranked New Zealand likeliest to win, with South Africa second. South Africa beat New Zealand in the final.\n\nThe same uncertainty applies at the Olympic sevens. While Argentina is favourite to win the men's tournament, there is still a 72% chance another team will take home the gold. Upsets should be expected - that is why watching sport is so enthralling.\n\nThe author acknowledges the assistance of Jensen Fiskin, whose data collection contributed to the forecasts included in this article.\n\nNiven Winchester does not work for, consult, own shares in or receive funding from any company or organisation that would benefit from this article, and has disclosed no relevant affiliations beyond their academic appointment.\n\n/Courtesy of The Conversation. They painted their cheeks with French flags, their hair with French colors. When the home team took the field for the first time at the Paris Games, a giant banner unrolled at one end of the stadium: Allez Les Bleus, the rallying cry of the French national teams.\n\nThey'd waited for years for this. The torch isn't yet lit, but the games have effectively begun. France opened play Wednesday in the rugby sevens tournament, the first athletic event for the host nation, which took place in front of an estimated 69,000 fans in the iconic Stade de France. Though the opening match ended in a 12-12 draw against a young American squad, it had the feel of a party, setting a promising tone for the rest of the Paris Games.\n\n\"Awesome,\" said American halfback Madison Hughes, competing in his third Olympics. \"That's what you want as an athlete. You want to perform in front of passionate fans who are really into what you're doing. Absolutely loved it.\"\n\nIt was a fitting opener. Rugby sevens is a fast-paced, truncated version of one of the world's most popular sports, and it's especially beloved in France. Every session of the rugby tournament is sold out.\n\n\"Rugby in France is hot,\" said Australia's Henry Hutchison, whose team won the first match of the tournament, 21-14, over Samoa. \"But it's also a world game, so there's so many people from around the world here.\"\n\nIt is among the most anticipated Olympic sports for locals and a marquee event for organizers, who chose to stage the tournament in the country's largest stadium. The 26-year-old Stade de France was built for the 1998 FIFA World Cup, serves as the home of the men's national soccer team and has hosted three rugby World Cups. Last year's World Cup, staged across France, averaged nearly 51,000 fans over the course of 48 matches.\n\nAlan Gilpin, chief executive of World Rugby, the sport's international governing body, said more than a half-million people will file through the stadium gates for the Olympic tournament, and rugby sevens was one of the highest demand events in Paris.\n\n\"We really believe this is the Olympic Games where rugby sevens comes of age,\" he said.\n\nAurelie Merle, the executive sports director of the Paris Games, said it was no accident that the athletic competition started Wednesday with both rugby sevens and the men's soccer tournament.\n\n\"This is the DNA of our Games ...\" he said. \"It's party time at this sport.\"\n\nAmerican Orrin Bizer walked out of the stadium tunnel Wednesday focused on what promised to be a consequential match against France. But he couldn't ignore the rumbling crowd and chuckled when he somehow spotted his sister amid the sea of French flags.\n\n\"Just seeing the atmosphere, it brought the biggest smile to my face,\" he said.\n\nThe crowd erupted barely three minutes into the match when France's Jordan Sepho crossed the goal line. It fell eerily silent by half, following a try by American Lucas Lacamp and Steve Tomasin's conversion, which gave the U.S. a 7-5 advantage. The ahhs and the oohs -- and occasional sacre bleus -- perfectly matched the rhythm of the fast-pace battle.\n\n\"That was a special crowd,\" Hughes said. \"Compared to Rio and then Tokyo, which had no crowd whatsoever, it's awesome for the Olympics to have that atmosphere.\"\n\nBarely 30 seconds into the second half, France's Rayan Rebadj's try put Les Bleus back on top, but then American Marcus Tupuola crossed the goal line with 5:08 remaining to tie the match at 12-12. Hughes missed the conversion that would've put the United States on top.\n\nThe Americans, who were knocked out in the quarterfinal round three years ago in Tokyo, weren't complaining about a draw against a talented team, as they hope to advance out of group play to the knockout rounds here.\n\n\"To draw with the host nation with all those fans in the stadium, just a test of who the boys are
